**Art. 202.** (1) Everyone is obliged to repair the damages that he has culpably caused to other persons in violation of the current provisions on the use and protection of waters and of the conditions of the issued permits.
(2) (Amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) Liability for damages under para. 1 does not release the person from payment for water abstraction, as well as from the costs of restoring the previous situation.
(3) In cases where the vegetation and animal life in water bodies - public state property, are damaged, the authority authorized to file claims for the repair of the damages is:
1. the Minister of Environment and Water, if the damages have occurred on the territory of more than one region;
2. the regional governor, if the damages have occurred on the territory of more than one municipality;
3. the mayor of the municipality, if the damages have occurred on the territory of one municipality.
(4) (Amend. - SG, No. 59 of 2007, in force from 01.03.2008) The claims under paras. 2 and 3 may also be filed by non-profit organizations whose object of

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 166 of 236

activity is environmental protection. In this case, the court shall ex officio apply Art. 26, para. 4 of the Civil Procedure Code.

**Art. 202a.** (New - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) The fines and property sanctions are paid into the account of the controlling authority specified in the act by which they are imposed.

**Art. 203.** (New - SG, No. 81 of 2000, amend. - SG, No. 84 of 2003 (*), amend. - SG, No. 59 of 2007, in force from 01.03.2008) Consumers and water users and users of wastewater discharge and treatment services and other services provided for in this Act - defaulting debtors, are liable for their obligations, and the service provider may request the issuance of an enforcement order under Art. 410, para. 1 of the Civil Procedure Code, regardless of the amount of the obligation.

**Additional Provisions**

**ยง 1.** (1) For the purposes of this Act:
1. "water regime" is a set of indicators characterizing the quantitative and qualitative state of the waters in the water bodies and its change in time and space;
2. (suppl. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water balance" is the ratio between precipitation, runoff, evaporation and filtration, characterizing the quantitative state of the waters by river basins or by water bodies;
3. "water resources" are the surface and groundwaters located in the water bodies that are used or can be used;
4. "water management balance" is the ratio between the available water resources and the water needs over time and place, determined with the aim of establishing the possibilities for satisfying the water needs;
5. "water management relations" are the relations that have arisen in the process of the activities of persons related to the use, restoration and protection of waters and water bodies;
6. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "aquifer" is one or more layers of rock or other geological strata located below the surface, which have sufficient porosity and permeability to allow a significant flow or abstraction of significant quantities of groundwater;
7. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water abstraction" covers

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 167 of 236

all activities related to the taking of water from water bodies;
8. "return waters" are the part of the water provided for use which is returned to water bodies;
9. "permissible yield" is the yield at a permissible drawdown of the water level, permissible temperature changes, permissible water quality and permissible impact on the environment;
10. (amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "operational resources of mineral waters" is the permissible and technically possible mean annual yield of mineral waters;
11. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "individual emission limits" are the values of the mass, expressed with certain parameters, concentration and/or emission level, determined in the permits for wastewater discharge when applying the combined approach, which must not be exceeded during a given period of time;
12. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "pollution" is any direct or indirect introduction into the air, water or soil as a result of human activity of substances or heat that may:
a) be harmful to human health or to the quality of aquatic ecosystems or of terrestrial ecosystems directly dependent on them;
b) cause material damage;
c) impair or impede the legally established use of the environment;
13. "earth's crust" is the part of the earth's crust accessible to human activity;
14. "springs" are the natural upward or downward, unconfined or confined outflow of groundwater to the earth's surface;
15. (rep. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006)
16. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "coastal floodplains of rivers" are the lands that are flooded:
a) within the boundaries of river corrections in populated areas and between the river and the dikes - where there are dikes;
b) (suppl. - SG, No. 58 of 2015) when the mean annual maximum water quantities with a 5 percent security or a recurrence of once every 20 years flow - for river sections with unbuilt corrections or protective facilities;
17. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 58 of 2015, amend. - SG, No. 17 of 2021) "mineral waters" are those specified in Appendix No. 2 to this Act, and in the other cases for which a certificate and/or a complex balneological assessment has been issued by the Ministry of Health;
18. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water monitoring" are measurements, observations and assessments for determining the state of the waters;
19. "dumps" are the accumulated technological waste from the exploration, extraction and/or primary processing of underground resources, with the exception of tailings ponds and slime ponds;
20. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "unforeseeable or

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 168 of 236

exceptional" are extraordinary circumstances caused by natural disasters or emergency situations, the occurrence of which cannot be foreseen and the consequences of which cannot be prevented;
21. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "mean water level" is the level of the water surface corresponding to the mean annual water quantity flowing through the riverbed;
22. "repeated" is a violation committed within one year of the entry into force of the penal decree by which the offender was punished for a violation of the same kind;
23. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "surface waters" are the waters on land, with the exception of groundwater, as well as transitional waters and coastal sea waters, except with regard to the chemical status, in which case the internal sea waters and the waters of the territorial sea are also included;
24. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "groundwaters" are all waters located below the earth's surface in the saturated zone, in direct contact with the ground strata;
25. "use" of a water body is any activity in it which, without being related to the abstraction of its waters, has the potential to affect the water regime;
26. (amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "appurtenant lands of reservoirs" are the lands that are flooded at the highest water level of the reservoir, determined for the overflow of a water quantity with a design security;
27. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "appurtenant lands of rivers" are the lands of the riverbeds that are flooded at the mean water level;
28. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "river basin" is the area of land from which, through a series of streams, rivers and lakes, the entire surface runoff flows into the sea at a single river mouth, estuary or delta;
29. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "transboundary waters" are surface or groundwaters that cross the border between the Republic of Bulgaria and one or more neighboring countries;
30. "water management" includes activities related to the use, protection and restoration of waters, as well as activities for protection from their harmful effects;
31. (amend. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "mouth" is any place where a watercourse discharges into another watercourse, lake or sea;
32. (new - SG, No. 42 of 2003, amend. - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009) "water supply system" is a set of facilities for the extraction of natural waters, their purification and/or disinfection to the required quality, storage, transportation, distribution and supply to the properties of consumers;
33. (new - SG, No. 42 of 2003, amend. - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 169 of 236

) "sewerage system" is a set of sewerage connections, street sewerage networks in urbanized territories, discharging collectors and treatment plants or treatment facilities, through which the discharge of wastewater and/or rainwater from the properties of consumers, their treatment and, if necessary, their disinfection to the required quality and their discharge into the respective water body is carried out;
34. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water body" is a permanent or temporary concentration of water with corresponding boundaries, volume and water regime in the earth's crust and in naturally or artificially created forms of relief, together with the lands appurtenant to them;
35. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "inland waters" are all standing or flowing waters on the surface of the land and all groundwaters landward of the baseline from which the width of the territorial sea is measured;
36. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water intended for human consumption" is surface or groundwater in its natural state or after treatment, intended for drinking, food preparation and other domestic purposes, supplied through a water supply system or from a cistern, in bottles, containers or other packaging, as well as waters used for the production of food, medicinal or cosmetic products or substances intended for human consumption, in case the quality of the water may affect the quality of the final products;
37. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water body" is a separate and significant part of surface or groundwater;
38. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "good ecological status" is the status of a surface water body, classified as such in accordance with the provisions of the ordinances under Art. 135, para. 1, items 9 and 14;
39. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "good quantitative status of groundwaters" is the status of a groundwater body determined under the conditions of the ordinance under Art. 135, para. 1, item 2;
40. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "good status of surface waters" is the status achieved for a surface water body when both its ecological and chemical status are at least "good";
41. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "good status of groundwaters" is the status achieved for a groundwater body when both its quantitative and chemical status are at least "good";
42. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "good chemical status of surface waters" is the chemical status of a surface water body in which the concentrations of pollutants do not exceed the established environmental quality standards;
43. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 170 of 236

) "good chemical status of groundwaters" is the chemical status of a groundwater body that meets the conditions established in the ordinance under Art. 135, para. 1, item 2;
44. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "good ecological potential" is the status of a heavily modified or artificial water body, classified as such in accordance with the provisions of the ordinances under Art. 135, para. 1, items 9 and 14;
45. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "lake" is a natural body of standing surface water formed in a depression of the relief;
46. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "environmental quality standard" is the concentration of certain pollutants or a group of pollutants in the water, sediments or biota which should not be exceeded for the purpose of protecting human health and the environment;
47. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "ecological status of surface water bodies" is an expression of the quality of the structure and functioning of the aquatic ecosystems associated with surface waters, classified in accordance with the provisions of the ordinances under Art. 135, para. 1, items 9 and 14;
48. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "emission norm" are the values of the mass, expressed through certain specific parameters, the concentration and/or level of the emission, which should not be exceeded during one or several periods of time;
49. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "regulation of emissions" is a specific restriction of emissions by determining emission norms or by determining restrictions or conditions for the effects, their nature or other characteristics of the emissions or the conditions of operation that affect the emissions;
50. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "pollutant" is any substance that may cause pollution, and especially the substances listed in the ordinance under Art. 135, para. 1, item 9;
51. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "artificial water body" is a surface water body created as a result of human activity;
52. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "quantitative status of groundwaters" is an indicator of the degree to which water abstraction or natural drainage from groundwaters affects the groundwater body;
53. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "combined approach" is the regulation of the discharge of wastewater into surface water bodies through the simultaneous application of the best available techniques and/or emission norms at the source of the wastewater, on the one hand, and the requirements for achieving the quality objectives of the waters in the surface water body - the recipient of the wastewater, on the other hand; in cases of diffuse sources of pollution, the regulation

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 171 of 236

includes, where necessary, the best ecological practices;
54. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "coastal sea waters" are surface waters landward of the coastline, every point of which is at a distance of one nautical mile seaward from the nearest point of the baseline from which the extent of the territorial sea is measured, extending, where appropriate, up to the outer limit of the transitional waters;
55. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "available groundwater resources" are the long-term mean annual recharge of the groundwater body from which the long-term mean annual flow rate necessary to achieve the environmental protection objectives under Art. 156a, para. 1, of the surface water bodies connected to the groundwater body is deducted, in order to avoid any significant deterioration in the ecological status of these waters, as well as to avoid any significant damage to the terrestrial ecosystems connected to them;
56. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "natural groundwater resources" are the long-term annual average value of the total recharge of the groundwater body;
57. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "indirect discharge of pollutants into groundwaters" is the discharge into groundwater bodies of pollutants through filtration through the soil or through the aeration zone;
58. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "hazardous substances" are substances or groups of substances that are classified as toxic, persistent and liable to bio-accumulate, as well as other substances or groups of substances that cause the same degree of concern;
59. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "surface water body" is a discrete and significant element of surface waters, such as a lake, a reservoir, a stream, a river or a canal, a part of a stream, a river or a canal, transitional waters or a stretch of coastal waters;
60. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "sub-basin" is the area of land from which, through a series of streams, rivers or lakes, the entire surface runoff flows into a specific point of a defined watercourse;
61. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "groundwater body" is a distinct volume of groundwater within one or more aquifers, characterized by a specific state of the groundwaters;
62. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "groundwater pollution threshold" is the concentration of a pollutant, a group of pollutants or a pollution indicator, the sustained exceedance of which creates a risk of not achieving a good chemical status of the groundwaters;
63. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "fresh waters" are waters that in their natural state have a low salt content and which can be used for drinking and domestic water supply;

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 172 of 236

64. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "transitional waters" are surface water bodies in the vicinity of river mouths which are partly saline as a result of their proximity to sea waters, but which are substantially influenced by the inflow of fresh water;
65. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "direct discharge of pollutants into groundwaters" is the discharge into groundwater bodies by pouring or injection of pollutants without filtration through the soil or through the aeration zone;
66. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "river basin management district" is an area of the land surface or sea, composed of one or more adjacent river basins together with their adjacent groundwaters and coastal waters;
67. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "river" is water on land, the greater part of which flows on the surface of the land, and in part of its course may flow under the surface of the land;
68. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "priority substances" are substances that pose a significant risk to the aquatic environment or through it are toxic to humans and ecotoxic to aquatic ecosystems and related terrestrial ecosystems and are determined in accordance with Art. 16 and Annex No. 10 to Directive 2000/60/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council;
69. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "individual drinking and domestic water supply" is the water supply of individual public and commercial sites where people permanently or temporarily reside or work and/or food, medicinal or cosmetic products are produced through individual own water abstraction facilities outside the water supply systems of populated areas and settlement formations;
70. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "heavily modified water body" is a surface water body whose characteristics have been substantially altered as a result of physical changes by human activity;
71. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "own needs of citizens" are the needs for water for domestic purposes, as well as for watering of animals and for irrigation within the boundaries of the own property, with the exception of the needs for water for carrying out an economic activity and exercising a profession or craft;
72. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "status of surface waters" is a general expression for the status of a surface water body, determined by the poorer of its ecological and chemical status;
73. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "status of groundwaters" is a general expression for the status of a groundwater body, determined by the poorer of its quantitative and chemical status;
74. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "water services" are all services for ensuring water for households, public institutions and for any

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 173 of 236

economic activity through water abstraction, impoundment, storage in reservoirs, treatment and supply of surface or groundwaters, as well as the collection, discharge and treatment with treatment facilities of wastewaters, which are then discharged into surface water bodies;
75. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "significant quantities of groundwaters" are water quantities for which it is technically possible to be depleted from the aquifer and which are of interest for practical use;
76. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "groundwater quality standard" is the environmental quality standard expressed as the concentration of a specific pollutant, group of pollutants or pollution indicator in groundwaters which should not be exceeded for the purpose of protecting human health and the environment;
77. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "significant and sustained upward trend" is any statistically and ecologically significant increase in the concentration of a pollutant, group of pollutants or change in a pollution indicator in groundwaters, for which it has been assessed that it is necessary to reverse the trend in accordance with Art. 156a, para. 1, item 2, letter "c";
78. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "conserved groundwater abstraction facility" is a facility for which abstraction has been temporarily suspended, it is not equipped for operation, but the possibility for its future operation is preserved;
79. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "liquidated groundwater abstraction facility" is a facility for which the possibility of natural or forced flow of water has been completely terminated;
80. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006, amend. and suppl. - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "water use" are water services together with any other human activity related to the abstraction of water, the use of water bodies and land use, for which, when characterizing the water bodies, carried out under the conditions of the ordinances under Art. 135, para. 1, items 2 and 9, it has been established that it has a significant impact on the state of the waters, and which are taken into account when implementing the economic analysis under Art. 192, para. 2, item 1;
81. (new - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) "riverbed" is an element of the relief in which a surface watercourse is temporarily or permanently formed and includes a river channel and coastal floodplains;
82. (new - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009) "water supply network" is an element of the water supply system in an urbanized territory, consisting of conduits and their appurtenant facilities for the distribution and transportation of water to consumers;
83. (new - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009) "sewerage network" is an element of the sewerage system in an urbanized territory, consisting of conduits and their appurtenant facilities for the discharge of wastewater from

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 174 of 236

consumers to the sewerage collectors outside the urbanized territories;
84. (new - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009, amend. - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "incidentally discovered mineral water" is mineral water discovered unexpectedly during a hydrogeological study or during the construction of a water abstraction facility for another purpose, carried out on the basis of a permit issued under this Act;
85. (new - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009) "regional WSS operator" is a WSS operator acting on the territory of more than one municipality;
86. (new - SG, No. 47 of 2009, in force from 23.06.2009) "municipal WSS operator" is a WSS operator acting on the territory of one municipality.
87. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "flood" is the temporary covering with water of a land area that is not normally covered with water, including from rivers, mountain streams and sea-induced floods in coastal areas; the flooding of land areas by sewerage systems is not a flood within the meaning of this Act;
88. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "flood risk" is the combination of the probability of a flood and the potential adverse consequences for human health, the environment, cultural heritage, technical infrastructure and economic activity, related to floods;
89. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "alluvial deposits" are a dynamic renewable stock of solid runoff, deposited in the riverbed during floods, with a grain size above 0.1 mm, composed of insoluble mineral and rock particles;
90. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "flood hazard" is the probability of flooding of certain territories; under flood hazard are those territories that, upon the occurrence of a flood with a certain probability, remain under water;
91. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010) "facilities, incl. sewerage systems of populated areas, settlement and resort formations, for which a permit is required under Art. 46, para. 1, item 3, letter "a", are those for which it is necessary to study, invest in design and build the whole or a part of the sewerage system and in the absence of an existing discharge of wastewater into surface waters;
92. (new - SG, No. 61 of 2010, amend. - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "facilities, incl. sewerage systems of populated areas, settlement and resort formations, for which a permit is required under Art. 46, para. 1, item 3, letter "b", are those that, after the necessary treatment, discharge wastewater at one or more places into surface waters; the necessary treatment of wastewater from sewerage systems of populated areas, settlement and resort formations is carried out within the periods specified in the ordinance under Art. 135, para. 1, item 13 and in accordance with the river basin management plans and the programs of measures;
93. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "household" are the spouses, persons living in actual cohabitation, as well as their children and relatives, if they live with them;
94. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015, amend. - SG, No. 55 of 2018) "dam" is a

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 175 of 236

water management system, including the water body, the dam wall, the facilities and the collecting diversions, as well as the land on which they are built;
95. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "dam wall operator" is a natural person hydro-specialist or a legal entity that has a hydro-specialist employee for carrying out the activities of management, maintenance and operation of dam walls and their appurtenant facilities, assigned to him by the owner;
95a. (new - SG, No. 55 of 2018) "structural integrity of dam walls" is their quality to remain with an intact mutual connection as such and in the systems with their appurtenant facilities - as a form, load-bearing capacity, support conditions, purpose and structural systems - under the action of the design loads and impacts, without being destroyed or significantly changed, without their connections being violated and without any of the design calculation models being changed; the preservation of the structural integrity of the dam wall and its appurtenant facilities ensures its operational suitability, i.e. for it to perform its purpose and not to allow an uncontrolled release of water from the reservoir and/or a violation of the design operational parameters of the dam;
95b. (new - SG, No. 55 of 2018) "breach of the structural integrity of a dam wall and its appurtenant facilities" is a breach of the compliance between the system of the dam wall and its appurtenant facilities and the design structural models of the elements of this system; this is a breach of the ability of the system to perform its purpose and, accordingly, a danger of an uncontrolled release of water from the reservoir and/or a violation of the design operational parameters of the dam;
95c. (new - SG, No. 55 of 2018) "critical infrastructure" is a concept within the meaning of ยง 1, item 15 of the additional provisions of the Disaster Protection Act;
96. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "pressure on the state of the waters" is any human activity that may have an adverse impact on the state of the waters;
97. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "water protection zone" is the territory of the catchment of a surface water body or the land surface above a groundwater body;
98. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "mineral water deposit" is a groundwater body or part of it, containing mineral waters of a uniform chemical composition and properties;
99. (new - SG, No. 58 of 2015) "pollution from a diffuse source" is pollution as a result of human activity, which is not a discharge of wastewater into surface waters and/or discharge of pollutants into groundwaters, concentrated at a specific point.
100. (new - SG, No. 98 of 2018, in force from 27.11.2018) "Mine waters" are

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021

---
Page 176 of 236

waters that flow to the surface from active or liquidated mining sites, including sites with geo-technological extraction, through mine or borehole workings.
101. (new - SG, No. 44 of 2020, in force from 14.05.2020) "Chemicals for the treatment of drinking and wastewater in the treatment processes" are flocculants, coagulants, biocides used for disinfection, and other products intended for drinking water treatment plants/facilities and wastewater treatment plants.
(2) (Suppl. - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) The definitions of the terms "internal sea waters", "territorial sea" and "continental shelf" in this Act are within the meaning of the Act on the Maritime Spaces, Inland Waterways and Ports of the Republic of Bulgaria.

**ยง 2.** In cases where this Act requires notification or announcement and where no explicit rules or the application of an explicitly defined procedure are provided for, the notification, respectively the announcement, shall be made under the procedure provided for in the Civil Procedure Code.

**ยง 2a.** (New - SG, No. 65 of 2006, in force from 11.08.2006) The water protection zones are protected in accordance with the standards and objectives determined by the act for the creation of the respective zone.

3. The ministries, departments and municipalities carry out measures for the protection of soil from pollution.
The Minister of Environment and Water exercises control for the protection of soil from pollution.
The Minister of Health exercises sanitary control over the state of the soil. He issues, in coordination with the Minister of Environment and Water, mandatory sanitary norms and rules for all departments, organizations and persons.
When exercising control under paras. 1, 2 and 3, the Ministry of Environment and Water and the Ministry of Health attract technically competent bodies and persons from other departments.

**ยง 28.** (1) For bringing the concession contracts concluded before the entry into force of this Act into conformity with the requirements of Art. 47, para. 9, the concessionaire may submit an application to the authority that signed the concession contract, within one month of the entry into force of this Act, which period is preclusive. With the application, the concessionaire declares the amount of the total annual operational resource that he wishes to be granted, and a schedule for its phased utilization in accordance with Art. 47, para. 10, item 3.
(2) For bringing the concession contracts concluded before the entry into force of this Act into conformity with the requirements of Art. 47, paras. 9 and 10, within a three-month period of the expiration of the period under para. 1, the authority that signed the concession contract submits to the Council of Ministers, respectively to the municipal council, a draft decision to give consent for the amendment and supplementation of the concession contract.
(3) The operational resource is determined in accordance with the orders of the Minister of Environment and Water for the approval of the operational resources that are in force as of the entry into force of this Act. When increasing the resource, the violation of acquired rights within the meaning of Art. 49, para. 3 is not allowed.
(4) When no application has been submitted within the period under para. 1, the authority that signed the concession contract submits, within the period under para. 2, to the Council of Ministers, respectively to the municipal council, a draft decision to give consent for the amendment and supplementation of the concession contract for its bringing into conformity with Art. 47, para. 10, items 1, 2 and 4.
(5) When the concessionaire does not conclude an additional agreement within a 6-month period of the adoption of the decisions under paras. 2 or 4, the concession contract is terminated by law, as of the date of expiration of this period.
(6) The terms for granting a concession for the extraction of mineral water, determined in the concession contracts concluded before the entry into force of this Act, may be extended by mutual agreement of the parties. (5) The assets under para. 1 are public state, respectively - public municipal property, from the entry of the decision to reduce the capital.

account of their capital and does not affect their financial result, established under the procedure of the Corporate Income Tax Act, with Art. 161 of the Corporate Income Tax Act applying only to assets that are not public state and/or public municipal property.

(8) The property and assets provided to the companies in liquidation or in insolvency proceedings, which are public state and/or public municipal property, are not subject to cash-out under the procedure of Art. 268, para. 1 of the Commercial Act, are not included in the insolvency estate under Art. 614, para. 1 of the Commercial Act and are not cashed out within the meaning of Art. 716 of the Commercial Act.

**ยง 30.** (In force from 24.09.2009) (1) The assignment of the activities under Art. 198o, para. 1 is carried out by concluding a contract between the chairman of the WSS association in accordance with a decision of its general meeting or the mayor of the municipality in accordance with a decision of the municipal council and the WSS operator acting on the respective consolidated territory as of the date of entry into force of this Act.

3. the investment obligations of the WSS operator for the construction of new WSS systems and facilities;

11. (amend. - SG, No. 17 of 2015, in force from 06.03.2015) the conditions and procedure for assuming and repaying financial obligations of the current WSS operator on the respective consolidated territory as of the date of entry into force of this Act and which are included in its business plan approved by the EWRC.

(10) Upon the selection of a new WSS operator, the employment relations of the employees of the previous WSS operator are regulated under the procedure of Art. 123 and 123a of the Labour Code.

5. a copy of a document for a paid fee in accordance with the tariff under Art. 72 of the Environmental Protection Act.
(3) The entry is carried out if the water abstraction facility:
1. exposes only one water body;
2. has a construction that does not allow the mixing of waters from several water bodies or the penetration of surface water into the water body through the behind-the-pipe space of the facility, and
3. is fit for operation.
(4) Within two months of the submission of the application, the director of the basin directorate shall check the documents under para. 2 and if the requirements of para. 3 are met, shall enter the facility in the respective register under Art. 118d, para. 3 of the Water Act.
(5) When the requirements of para. 3 are not met, the director of the basin directorate refuses entry in the respective register under Art. 118d, para. 3 of the Water Act and prescribes the liquidation of the facility.
(6) The permitting of water abstraction from registered facilities under para. 1 is carried out under the conditions and procedure of the Water Act.
(7) (Amend. - SG, No. 102 of 2020, in force from 27.11.2020) The owners of wells for satisfying the own needs of citizens located within the boundaries of populated areas and settlement formations, for which no applications for entry in the register under Art. 118d, para. 3, item 5 of the Water Act have been submitted by November 27, 2018, shall submit an application by November 28, 2022, to the respective basin directorate for the entry of the facilities in the register. The application contains the information for the registration of a constructed well, determined in the ordinance under Art. 135, para. 1, item 2 of the Water Act.
(8) (Amend. - SG, No. 102 of 2020, in force from 27.11.2020) The application under para. 7 may also be submitted through the respective mayor of a municipality, mayor of a district, mayor of a mayoralty or the mayor's deputy at the location of the well. The mayors and mayor's deputies shall issue an incoming number for each received application and every 14 days shall hand over to the respective basin directorate the applications received during this period.

**ยง 42.** The groundwater abstraction facilities built by December 23, 2016, for which no construction documents have been issued, are tolerated constructions under the Spatial Development Act and are not subject to removal and prohibition of use when they are entered in the register under Art. 118d, para. 3 of the Water Act.

Source: "Ciela" Legal Information Systems 05/11/2021
